0:000> !address -?

!address {-? | -help}      - prints this help
!address <address>         - prints available information about the region
                               of the memory space containing the specified address
!address -summary          - prints only summary information

!address [-f:F1,F2,...] [{[-o:{csv | tsv | 1}] | [-c:"Command"]}]
   - when used with no switches, !address displays the virtual memory map with all the regions that could be
     classified given the available information and the extension capabilities; an asterisk as the first
     character in the output marks the beginning of a new region, followed by lines that describe the
     blocks that belong to the same region (all blocks having the same allocation base)

   -f:F1,F2,...            - filters the output according to various criteria; when filtering is on, the
                               region delimiters (*) are not used; all filters in the list are AND-combined:
       Unk                     - unclassified regions ('busy' regions that could not be classified better)
       Free                    - 'free' regions (not 'busy': neither committed, nor reserved)
       Image                   - regions used for images
       Stack                   - regions used for stacks
       Teb                     - regions used for thread execution blocks
       Peb                     - regions used for process execution blocks
       Heap                    - regions used by heaps (segments, virtual blocks, and other heap regions)
       PageHeap                - regions used for page heap
       FileMap                 - regions used for memory mapped files (live targets only)
       Other                   - other known regions

       MEM_COMMIT              - regions with MEM_COMMIT state
       MEM_FREE                - regions with MEM_FREE state (same as 'Free')
       MEM_RESERVE             - regions with MEM_RESERVE state

       MEM_IMAGE               - regions of type MEM_IMAGE
       MEM_MAPPED              - regions of type MEM_MAPPED
       MEM_PRIVATE             - regions of type MEM_PRIVATE

       PAGE_NOACCESS           - regions with PAGE_NOACCESS protection
       PAGE_READONLY           - regions with PAGE_READONLY protection
       PAGE_READWRITE          - regions with PAGE_READWRITE protection
       PAGE_WRITECOPY          - regions with PAGE_WRITECOPY protection
       PAGE_EXECUTE            - regions with PAGE_EXECUTE protection
       PAGE_EXECUTE_READ       - regions with PAGE_EXECUTE_READ protection
       PAGE_EXECUTE_READWRITE  - regions with PAGE_EXECUTE_READWRITE protection
       PAGE_EXECUTE_WRITECOPY  - regions with PAGE_EXECUTE_WRITECOPY protection
       PAGE_GUARD              - regions with PAGE_GUARD protection
       PAGE_NOCACHE            - regions with PAGE_NOCACHE protection
       PAGE_WRITECOMBINE       - regions with PAGE_WRITECOMBINE protection

   -o                      - controls the output format as follows:
       1                       - prints results in bare format (to be used in .foreach)
       csv                     - prints results as comma-separated-values
       tsv                     - prints results as tab-separated-values

   -c:"Command" [-e]     - executes a custom command for each memory region. Command must be enclosed in quotes.
                               Placeholders %1 to %7 will be replaced with the content of the corresponding 
                               fields for every line in the output: %1 is the base address, %2 is the 
                               end address+1, %3 is the region size, etc. Quotes and backslashes must be
                               escaped using "\". Multiple commands separated by semicolons ";" are not 
                               supported.
                               The optional -e switch enables echoing of the command before execution.
                               See usage example below.

Usage example in .foreach:
       .foreach /ps 6 (baseaddr {!address /o:1 /f:MEM_MAPPED}) { db baseaddr l2 }


Usage examples with custom command:
       Search for the string MZ in all image regions:
           !address /f:Image /c:"s -a %1 %2 \"MZ\""
       Search for the wide string "true" (including quotes) in all heap regions:
           !address /f:heap /c:"s -u %1 L?%3 \"\\\"true\\\"\""
       Execute !dh on the base address for each image region:
           !address /f:image /c:"!dh %1"

0:000> !address -?

!address {-? | -help}      - prints this help
!address <address>         - prints available information about the region
                               of the memory space containing the specified address
!address -summary          - prints only summary information

!address [-f:F1,F2,...] [{[-o:{csv | tsv | 1}] | [-c:"Command"]}]
   - when used with no switches, !address displays the virtual memory map with all the regions that could be
     classified given the available information and the extension capabilities; an asterisk as the first
     character in the output marks the beginning of a new region, followed by lines that describe the
     blocks that belong to the same region (all blocks having the same allocation base)

   -f:F1,F2,...            - filters the output according to various criteria; when filtering is on, the
                               region delimiters (*) are not used; all filters in the list are AND-combined:
       Unk                     - unclassified regions ('busy' regions that could not be classified better)
       Free                    - 'free' regions (not 'busy': neither committed, nor reserved)
       Image                   - regions used for images
       Stack                   - regions used for stacks
       Teb                     - regions used for thread execution blocks
       Peb                     - regions used for process execution blocks
       Heap                    - regions used by heaps (segments, virtual blocks, and other heap regions)
       PageHeap                - regions used for page heap
       FileMap                 - regions used for memory mapped files (live targets only)
       Other                   - other known regions

       MEM_COMMIT              - regions with MEM_COMMIT state
       MEM_FREE                - regions with MEM_FREE state (same as 'Free')
       MEM_RESERVE             - regions with MEM_RESERVE state

       MEM_IMAGE               - regions of type MEM_IMAGE
       MEM_MAPPED              - regions of type MEM_MAPPED
       MEM_PRIVATE             - regions of type MEM_PRIVATE

       PAGE_NOACCESS           - regions with PAGE_NOACCESS protection
       PAGE_READONLY           - regions with PAGE_READONLY protection
       PAGE_READWRITE          - regions with PAGE_READWRITE protection
       PAGE_WRITECOPY          - regions with PAGE_WRITECOPY protection
       PAGE_EXECUTE            - regions with PAGE_EXECUTE protection
       PAGE_EXECUTE_READ       - regions with PAGE_EXECUTE_READ protection
       PAGE_EXECUTE_READWRITE  - regions with PAGE_EXECUTE_READWRITE protection
       PAGE_EXECUTE_WRITECOPY  - regions with PAGE_EXECUTE_WRITECOPY protection
       PAGE_GUARD              - regions with PAGE_GUARD protection
       PAGE_NOCACHE            - regions with PAGE_NOCACHE protection
       PAGE_WRITECOMBINE       - regions with PAGE_WRITECOMBINE protection

   -o                      - controls the output format as follows:
       1                       - prints results in bare format (to be used in .foreach)
       csv                     - prints results as comma-separated-values
       tsv                     - prints results as tab-separated-values

   -c:"Command" [-e]     - executes a custom command for each memory region. Command must be enclosed in quotes.
                               Placeholders %1 to %7 will be replaced with the content of the corresponding 
                               fields for every line in the output: %1 is the base address, %2 is the 
                               end address+1, %3 is the region size, etc. Quotes and backslashes must be
                               escaped using "\". Multiple commands separated by semicolons ";" are not 
                               supported.
                               The optional -e switch enables echoing of the command before execution.
                               See usage example below.

Usage example in .foreach:
       .foreach /ps 6 (baseaddr {!address /o:1 /f:MEM_MAPPED}) { db baseaddr l2 }


Usage examples with custom command:
       Search for the string MZ in all image regions:
           !address /f:Image /c:"s -a %1 %2 \"MZ\""
       Search for the wide string "true" (including quotes) in all heap regions:
           !address /f:heap /c:"s -u %1 L?%3 \"\\\"true\\\"\""
       Execute !dh on the base address for each image region:
           !address /f:image /c:"!dh %1"
